Bahrami grew up in Iran, where he fell in love with tennis despite limited access to proper facilities and equipment. He often played with improvised rackets made from frying pans or dustbin lids. His natural talent was evident early on, and he quickly became one of Iranâ€™s top players. However, his career was derailed by the 1979 Iranian Revolution, which led to a ban on tennis as it was considered a Western and bourgeois pastime.
